title": "Mexican fishballs in tomato sauce",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Mexican fishballs in tomato sauce a fish recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#masaharina #mexicanfishballsintomatosauce #mildmexicanpassata #basa #parsley #whitebread #tabascosauce #egg #fry #whitefish #oliveoil \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Masa harina has such a wonderful unique flavour that it's worth the effort to try and get hold of it\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1487\n|PortionCalories = 743\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 2\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 30 minutes \n |PrepTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Mexican fishballs in tomato sauce recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Masa, masa, masa!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Masa Harina is The Boss.  Makes such a difference to this recipe.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nMasa harina has such a wonderful unique flavour that it's worth the effort to try and get hold of it.  Most [[:Category:Tex-Mex ingredients (supplier)|Mexican ingredient suppliers]] stock it.\n\nMake this with any [[white fish]], [[Basa|basa]] would be my choice as a flavoursome, economical and sustainable fish. Most supermarkets now stock it.\n\n'''fishballs'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 250g [[Basa|basa]] fillets, roughly chopped\n| 1 [[Spring onion|spring onion]], roughly chopped\n| About 200 ml of dried breadcrumbs or 2 slices of [[White bread|white bread]], finely chopped\n| 1 raw [[egg]]\n| A big handful of chopped [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n'''to coat'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 50g [[Masa harina]]\n}}\n'''for [[Frying|frying]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 tablespoon of butter, 2 tablespoons of [[Olive oil]]\n}}\n''' serve and garnish with'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| [[Tabasco sauce]] or [[Louisiana Hot Pepper Sauce|Louisiana hot pepper sauce]]\n| 1 Sliced [[Roasted red peppers|roasted red peppers]]\n| 150 ml [[Sofrito]] or [[Tomato sauce for pizza]]\n| 1 Finely chopped [[Hard-boiled eggs|hard-boiled egg]]\n| 10 [[Olives]]\n| 1 tablespoon freshly chopped [[Parsley|parsley]]\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>>\nImage:Mexican fishballs frying.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Frying the fishballs\nImage:Mexican fishballs in tomato sauce ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The original ingredients - the recipe has since been slightly modified\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add all of the fishball ingredients into a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade and blitz to a rough paste.\n| Roll into small balls and leave to chill in the [[Fridge|fridge]] for an hour or so\n| Add a few tablespoons of [[Masa harina|masa harina]] to a large plate, only a little is needed so don't waste it as I did!\n| Roll the balls in [[Masa harina|masa harina]] to coat.\n| Heat the butter and oil in a large frying pan and shallow [[Fry|fry]] until browned and crispy on the outside\n| Serve with [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]] and the garnishes of your choice.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nFor two people this was served with [[Mild Mexican passata]], a portion of pasta for one (100g [[dried pasta]] and a chopped boiled egg.  A very unique and very nice recipe!\n===Variations===\nIf you can get then, fresh [[Poblano chillies|poblano chillies]], [[Roasted|roasted]] and sliced would go well with this as they fairly mild.\n\nI have added a handful of finely chopped [[dried shrimp]] to the mixture.  Not authentic, but adds a nice fishy touch to fishcakes and similar recipes.\n\nWhen I made this I tinkered with the tomato sauce and came up with a separate recipe (if you can call it a recipe), [[Mild Mexican passata]].  It went really well with the fishballs as it had a slightly bitter, chocolatey note.\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you can't get [[Masa harina|masa harina]], coarsely [[Ground|ground]] [[Yellow cornmeal|yellow cornmeal]] would be ok, but it would not have the same distinct flavour.\n\nWhen I made this, the paste was far too wet, so I added another handful of dried breadcrumbs, a little masa, remixed it and set it in a sieve for an hour to drain a little excess liquid.  The result was still quite liquid, but the end result was excellent.  \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#masaharina #mexicanfishballsintomatosauce #mildmexicanpassata #basa #parsley #whitebread #tabascosauce #egg #fry #whitefish #oliveoil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

flavours to mingle\n| Heat the [[ghee]] in a [[frying]] pan or [[wok]]\n| Add the mince and [[fry]]  until done to your liking\n| Pour off any excess [[fat]]\n| Add the juice from half an [[orange]], mince.\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Main I think that this is pretty close.  It works with [[chicken]] as well as [[beef]].\n\nI deliberately wanted a dry mix to put into taco shells, as the ''[[sauce]]'' would be provided by [[guacamole]], [[sour cream]] or [[yogurt]]\n\n\n'''Main ingredients'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 packet of [[taco shells]] or [[taco trays]]\n| 225 g (1/2 lb) lean minced [[beef]]\n| 1 [[red pepper]], chopped finely\n| Juice from &#189; an [[orange]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[ghee]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[tomato puree]]\n}}\n'''For the dry spice mix'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 teaspoon dried smoked chillies such as [[chipotle]]:\n| 1/4 of a teaspoon of [[black peppercorns]]\n| 5 cm (1/2\") [[cinnamon stick]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[white cumin]] seeds\n| 1 teaspoon [[black cumin]] seeds\n| 1/2 a teaspoon [[dried minced garlic]]\n| [[Sea salt]] to taste\n| &#189; teaspoon of [[dried]] [[oregano]]\n| Good pinch of [[salt]] or 1 tablespoon of juice from [[preserved lemons]] - if using the latter, add in step 3 \n}}\n'''For garnishing'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| Four [[spring onions]], [[chopped on the diagonal]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Grind all of the dry [[spices]] in a [[coffee grinder]]\n| Tip the mince and the [[chopped red peppers]] into a bowl\n| Add the dry [[spices]] and [[tomato puree]] and mix them together by kneading the mince\n| If you have the time, leave for an hour in a cool place for the flavours to mingle\n| Heat the [[ghee]] in a [[frying]] pan or [[wok]]\n| Add the mince and [[fry]]  until done to your liking\n| Pour off any excess [[fat]]\n| Add the juice from &#189; an [[orange]]\n| [[Stir fry]] for a few more minutes and pour away any excess liquid\n| If desired, put in half the of the spring onions during the last minute of cooking (as in the photo), kill the heat and serve immediately.\n| Arrange on a hot plate and sprinkle with all of/the rest of the chopped [[spring onions]] over the filled taco shells\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[taco shells]] (or the really neat [[taco trays]]), [[sour cream]], [[guacamole]], [[pickled jalape\u00f1os]] and a salsa such as [[sweet potato salsa]]\n===Variations===\n\nTry [[chicken]] fillets or [[shredded]] [[beef]] steak instead\n\nSprinkle with grated [[Monterey Jack]] or [[Cheddar cheese]]\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Beef]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:North American recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#spices #mincedbeeffortacos #beef #chicken #tacotrays #orange #tomatopuree #ghee #guacamole #springonions #tacoshells </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

It made more sense to measure the chillies by volume rather than weight\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1179\n|PortionCalories = 12\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Servings: 450 - Makes about 4 [[Pints|pints]]\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 5 hours, 40 minutes incl cooling time\n |PrepTime = 5 hours, 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 25 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Orange biter (chili sauce) recipe 1.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Superb</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I remember this - I can still taste it!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Orange biter (chili sauce) recipe.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Simmering chillies]]\nAnother one of my [[Chili sauce|chili sauce]] creations!\n\nIt made more sense to measure the chillies by volume rather than weight.  The chili flakes I have are slightly oily and would be heavier than truly dried chillies.\n\nWear rubber gloves and work in a well ventilated kitchen when handling this amount of chillies.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 250 ml [[Malt vinegar|malt vinegar]]\n| 350 ml [[red wine vinegar]]\n| 250 ml [[Juice|juice]] from [[Preserved lemons|preserved lemons]] (basically very salty lemon juice)\n| 200 ml water\n| 100 g [[Jaggery|jaggery]]\n| 2 pints (by volume) of Turkish [[Chilli flakes|chilli flakes]]\n| 2 [[Oranges|oranges]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add everything but the [[Oranges|oranges]] to a large pot and bring to the [[Boil|boil]]\n| Reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 15 minutes, stirring often\n| Meanwhile, halve the [[Oranges|oranges]] and extract the [[Juice|juice]]\n| Stir the [[Chilli|chilli]] mix to ensure the [[Jaggery|jaggery]] has dissolved\n| Mix in the [[Orange juice|orange juice]] and add the [[Orange|orange]] skins (they will be removed and discarded later)\n| [[Simmer]] the mixture for another 5 minutes\n| Remove from the heat and leave for 4 hours\n| Remove and discard the [[Orange|orange]] skins, being careful not to waste too much [[Sauce|sauce]]\n| Add the mixture to a food processor with a sharp blade and reduce to a [[Puree|puree]]\n| Decant into [[Sterilised jars|sterilised jars]] and store in a dark place for 3 months\n}}\n===Chef's tip===\nThis is very good - though it never got its 3 months rest!  Only 1 jar left now.\n===Third batch===\nSee [[Talk:Orange biter (hot chili sauce)|comments]] page for details of the even more successful 3rd batch\n==See also==\n* [[Chilli sauce|Many other chilli sauce recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#oranges #orange #simmer #juice #jaggery #pints #boil #chilisauce #maltvinegar #puree #sterilisedjars </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Picadillo",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Picadillo a beef recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#picadillo #beef #bellpepper #tomatoes #garlic #potato #vegetables #spanishrice #unusualrecipes #browning #diced \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Picadillo is a dish mainly consisting of ground beef typically found in Puerto Rico, Cuba, Mexico, and other Latin American countries\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2856\n|PortionCalories = 476\n|DatePublished=8th December 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 50 minutes\n|PrepTime = 10 minutes\n|CookTime = 40 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Picadillo recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Home cooking!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">We love this</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nPicadillo is a dish mainly consisting of ground [[Beef|beef]] typically found in Puerto Rico, Cuba, Mexico, and other Latin American countries. In Mexico and Puerto Rico it is sometimes used as a filling, such as for [[Tacos|tacos]], and can be mixed with [[Vegetables|vegetables]]. It can also be prepared as a type of stew. In most other Latin American countries it consists of a common table from where people pick small beef pieces or other food such as [[French fries|french fries]]. The name comes from the Spanish word, \"picar\" which means \"to mince\" or \"to chop\".\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500 g (1 lb 2 oz) of lean [[minced]] [[Beef|beef]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 4 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], chopped\n| 284 ml (&frac12; pint) [[Beef stock|beef stock]] \n| 1 large [[Green bell pepper|green bell pepper]],deseeded and chopped\n| 3 large russet [[Potato|potato]], cubed, bite size\n| 1 400 g (14.5 oz) tin [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] together with the juice\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Oil|oil]]\n| 1/8 teaspoon [[Sea salt|sea salt]] \n| 2 tablespoons of [[Tex-Mex seasoning]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a large, heavy pan, heat the [[Oil|oil]] to medium-high heat. Add the [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Bell pepper|bell pepper]] and seasoning to the pan.\n| When the [[Bell pepper|bell pepper]] starts to discolour, add to it ground [[Beef|beef]], stirring to break up large pieces and [[Brown|brown]] evenly, about 7 minutes. \n| As [[Meat|meat]] is [[Browning|browning]], add [[Potato|potato]], [[Beef|beef]] broth and [[Diced|diced]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]. \n| [[Simmer]] until the potato is cooked and the picadillo has thickened, stirring occasionally.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[Spanish rice]] and tortilla.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Cuban recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#picadillo #beef #bellpepper #tomatoes #garlic #potato #vegetables #spanishrice #unusualrecipes #browning #diced </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Picante guacamole recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#guacamole #cup #avocados #picanteguacamole #limes #garlic #onions #recipesfromothersites #juice #serrano #hassavocados \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This guacamole recipe is courtesy of Mextrade.co.uk and originates from Picante Mexican Grill, Blackfriars\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 726\n|PortionCalories = 181\n|DatePublished=3rd June 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Picante guacamole recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">\ud83e\udd51\ud83e\udd51\ud83e\udd51</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Spicy dip!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis [[guacamole]] recipe is courtesy of [[Mextrade.co.uk]] and originates from the now extinct Picante Mexican Grill, Blackfriars, London\n\nProper [[Guacamole|guacamole]] is absolutely glorious, when made the traditional way with the right ingredients. Using [[Serrano]] [[Chilli pepper|chilli pepper]] adds a slightly nutty flavour that pairs very nicely with has [[Avocados|avocados]]. We have tried many brands over the years and exclusively use La Coste\u00f1a for their unbeatable flavour.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 [[Hass avocados]] (medium size)\n| &#8531; [[Cup|cup]] fresh [[Tomato|tomato]], chopped (about 1 medium)\n| &#8531; [[Cup|cup]] white [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped \n| 1 medium [[Clove|clove]] [[Garlic|garlic]], very finely chopped-ideally use a [[Garlic press|garlic press]]\n| &#8531; [[Cup|cup]] [[Coriander|coriander]], finely chopped (cut off steams just below 2nd leaves)\n| &#189; [[Lime|lime]], juiced\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 3 teaspoons La Coste\u00f1a Serrano escabeche (the [[Marinate|marinate]] liquid from the tin) \n| 2 [[Serrano chillies|serrano chillies]] finely chopped\n| Pinch [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add all of the ingredients to a bowl\n| Using a fork, mix for a minutes to ensure everything is evenly distributed\n| Serve immediately\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nDo not use any other [[Avocados|avocados]] than Haas as they do not have the correct texture or flavour to make [[Guacamole|guacamole]], Haas are generally very dark in colour and have rough skin.\n\nOnly use perfectly ripe [[Avocados|avocados]], if the flesh is too firm or grey, it doesn't belong in [[Guacamole|guacamole]]. Grey avocados belong in the compost heap.\n\n[[Limes]] may yield variable amounts of [[Juice|juice]], so follow your taste buds. I personally prefer less [[Lime juice|lime juice]], but it is a key [[Ingredient|ingredient]], as it acts a natural [[Preservative|preservative]] and prevents the [[Avocado|avocado]] flesh from turning colour.\n\n''Jason Coolbaugh - Picante Grill''\n\n{{GuacamoleRecipes}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:MexTrade.co.uk recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n===Recipe source===\n{{Template:RecipeCourtesyOfMexTrade.co.uk}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#guacamole #cup #avocados #picanteguacamole #limes #garlic #onions #recipesfromothersites #juice #serrano #hassavocados </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

778\n|DatePublished=9th November 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  10 minutes\n|PrepTime =  3 minutes\n|CookTime =  7 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Popcorn baked beans with sundried tomatoes recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Well I never!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">The oddest thing, but really good.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]]</span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Morrisons mixed bean salad.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Morrisons' mixed bean salad]]\n\nWell these [[Beans|beans]] are not [[Baked|baked]], they're [[Popped|popped]], like [[Popcorn|popcorn]] but they taste better than any tinned [[Baked beans|baked beans]] and only take 10 minutes from start to finish.\n\nI got the idea of [[Frying|frying]] the [[Beans|beans]] from one of Jamie Oliver's 15 minute meal TV programs but instead of making a [[Salad|salad]] I wanted to make luxury [[Baked beans|baked beans]].\n\nThis is a brilliant recipe to mess about with and is ideal for using up odd leftovers.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 400g can of [[Mixed bean salad|mixed bean salad]]\n| 1 whole bottled [[Red pepper|red pepper]], chopped and 2 tablespoons of the [[Oil|oil]] from the jar\n| [[Freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sundried tomato paste|sundried tomato paste]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]]\n| Pinch of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Drain the [[Beans|beans]] and rinse them a few times and allow them to drain well\n| Heat the [[Red pepper|red pepper]] [[Oil|oil]] in a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] over a high heat\n| Add a pinch of [[Black pepper|black pepper]] to the [[Oil|oil]] and swill it around the pan\n| Get a cover for the pan as it will spit violently when you add the [[Beans|beans]]\n| Very carefully tip the [[Beans|beans]] into the [[Frying pan|frying pan]] and cover quickly\n| Jiggle the pan to keep the [[Beans|beans]] turning over, ideally while holding the cover an inch away from the pan so they don't start to [[Steam|steam]] yet\n| After a minute or so, the [[Beans|beans]] will pop like [[Popcorn|popcorn]], crisping the skins and revealing a fluffy core\n| Once most of the [[Beans|beans]] have [[Popped|popped]] and the pan has calmed down a little, stir in the  chopped [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Sundried tomato paste|sundried tomato paste]] and [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]]\n| Mix well, reduce the heat and cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 3 or 4 minutes\n| If they look too dry, add a splash of liquid.  You could use water, [[Stock|stock]] , [[Wine|wine]] or [[Beer|beer]].  I used a splash of Stella [[Lager|lager]] to loosen them\n| Serve immediately\n}}\n===Variations===\nUse any variety of canned [[Beans|beans]] and practically anything you can think of.  Bottled [[Peppers|peppers]] are good because they don't require any cooking, however you could add fresh peppers for a little crunch, finely [[Chopped spring onions|chopped spring onions]], chillies, oh the list is endless!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beans #sundriedtomatopaste #bakedbeans #tomatopuree #peppers #popcorn #popped #redpepper #unusualrecipes #frying #steam </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Pork steaks in calvados",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Porksteaks in calvados recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#calvados #marinade #pork #grill #haricotbeans #duckfat #masaharina #oliveoil #griddle #fridge #sauce \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Holidaying in France, we discovered what a marvellous marinade calvados was for pork\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1293\n|PortionCalories = 646\n|DatePublished=19th September 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  1 hour, 5 minutes\n|CookTime =  10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Pork steaks in calvados recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">\ud83e\udd69 + \ud83c\udf77 = \ud83e\udd2d</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">\ud83e\udd2d\ud83e\udd2d\ud83e\udd2d</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nWhile on holiday in [[France]] recently we discovered what a marvellous [[Marinade|marinade]] [[Calvados|calvados]] (''apple brandy'') was for [[Pork|pork]] steaks, so once home we tried a sort of [[Tex-Mex|tex-mex]] version to accompany the [[French]] [[Haricot beans|haricot beans]] cooked in [[Duck fat|duck fat]] - very Basque!\n\nTHe meal was fantastic but the presentation could have been improved with a little green, maybe a [[Sweet Pepper|sweet pepper]]?\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 x 160g boneless  [[Pork|pork]] steaks\n| 50 ml (or so) of [[Calvados|calvados]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Tex-Mex rub|tex-mex rub]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 6 tablespoon [[Masa Harina|masa harina]] - fine or coarse [[Yellow cornmeal|yellow cornmeal]] works almost as well for this\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Tenderise the meat with a [[ Swiss steak|meat tenderiser tool]] if you have one\n* Place the steaks in a [[Lock and Lock box]] together with the [[Calvados|calvados]] and the [[Tex-Mex rub|tex-mex rub]] - \n* Leave to [[Marinade|marinade]] in the [[Fridge|fridge]] for an hour or more if possible shaking now and then to ensure a good cover\n* Preheat the [[Grill|grill]] or [[Griddle pan|griddle pan]] - I used a Breville electric grill\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Drain the [[Pork|pork]] steaks and discard the [[Marinade|marinade]] - it could be used for making a [[Sauce|sauce]] but I didn't need gravy this time\n| Add the [[Masa Harina|masa harina]] to a large place and press the steaks into the [[Flour|flour]] to coat\n| [[Oil]] the [[Grill|grill]] with a little [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and [[Griddle|griddle]] for about 8 minutes - turning once if not using a double-sided griddle\n| Leave to [[Rest for|rest for]] 5 minutes\n| Serve\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Masa grilled pork steaks.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Steaks griddled in masa harina, ready to rest\nImage:Pork marinading in calvados.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Marinating in calvados\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nWe had this with Basque [[Haricot beans|haricot beans]] in [[Duck fat|duck fat]] - very healthy!\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#calvados #marinade #pork #grill #haricotbeans #duckfat #masaharina #oliveoil #griddle #fridge #sauce </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

The Cool [[Chili|chili]] co sell this if you are have difficulty finding it in the Uk.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 5 [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 450 g (1 lb) [[Pork tenderloin fillet|pork tenderloin fillet]], cut into small cubes\n| &frac14; teaspoon [[Pepper|pepper]]\n| [[Chicken stock]] or water\n| 1 teaspoon freshly [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Dried oregano|dried oregano]]\n| 3 [[Cloves|cloves]], [[Ground|ground]]\n| 5 fresh [[Chillies|chillies]], de-seeded and chopped into rings\n| 2 cups [[Dried|dried]] [[Hominy|hominy]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Re-constitute the [[Dried|dried]] [[Hominy|hominy]] by soaking overnight in lightly [[Salted|salted]] water.\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| On a high heat, add the [[Oil|oil]] to a large saucepan and [[Brown|brown]] the [[Meat|meat]] in small batches, remove and reserve\n| Add the [[Ground pepper|ground pepper]] to the [[Oil|oil]], reduce the heat and gently [[Simmer|simmer]] the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] until translucent, about 5 minutes\n| Add enough [[Stock|stock]] or water to cover the [[Meat|meat]] by at least 5cm (2\")\n| Add the remaining ingredients and [[Simmer|simmer]], covered, for about 2 hours, topping up with [[Stock|stock]] or water if necessary.\n| Season to taste with [[Salt|salt]] and extra [[Pepper|pepper]] if required.\n}}\n===Variations===\nFor extra flavour and to bulk out the [[Soup|soup]], add 1/4 of a [[Cabbage|cabbage]], finely chopped after the first hour of cooking.\n===Chef's notes===\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Popcorn recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#hominy #pozolesouprecipe #dried #simmer #stock #garlic #soup #groundcumin #cabbage #chillies #miseenplace </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Both are a must for all things Mexican and much more.  The book is available from their website.\n\nThis dish is very similar in taste to the Indian dish, Garlic chilli prawns, I trust you will enjoy it\n\n'''..for the [[prawns]]..'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500 g (1 lb) of fresh [[peeled prawns]]\n| 25 g (1 oz) [[butter]] for [[frying]]\n| 4 cloves of [[Garlic]]\n| [[Sea salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n'''..for the [[sauce]]..'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 2 medium [[onions]], peeled and chopped\n| 2 cloves of [[Garlic]]\n| 1 large (400g) can of peeled plum [[tomatoes]], blitzed in a [[food processor]].\n| 2 tablespoons [[tomato puree]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[lime]] [[zest]]\n| 1 can or small bottle of [[Pepsi]] Original. Not lo-cal, diet or odd-flavoured versions)\n| 2 [[chipotle chillies]], finely chopped\n| 2 [[chile de Arbole]], finely chopped\n| [[Sea salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n'''..to garnish..'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| [[Wedges]] of fresh [[lime]]\n| A handful of chopped [[parsley]], finely chopped\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Prawns 'n' Pepsi reduced.jpg|the sauce...reduced\nImage:Prawns 'n' Pepsi sauce.jpg|The sauce\nImage:Prawns 'n' Pepsi recipe.jpg|Prawns 'n' Pepsi\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| '''The [[sauce]]'''\n| [[Fry]] the [[onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] for 4 minutes in a little [[olive oil]] until they are translucent\n| Add the pressed [[tomatoes]], [[tomato puree]], chopped [[chillies]], [[lime]] zest, [[Pepsi]], [[salt]] and [[pepper]] then [[simmer]] vigorously for 25 minutes or until reduced to a thick [[sauce]].\n| '''The [[prawns]]'''\n| [[Fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] in the [[butter]] until it takes a little colour\n| Add the [[prawns]] and [[fry]] them until they turn pink\n| Season to taste with [[salt]] and [[pepper]]\n| Mix the [[sauce]] into the [[prawns]], combine well and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[plain boiled rice]] and [[peas and peppers]]\n===Variations===\n\nIf you can afford it, try chunks of [[monkfish]] or even [[lobster]].\n\n===Any left overs?===\n\nYes? - then make [[Prawn 'n' Pepsi flan]]! \n\n===Chef's tip===\n\nIf you are using [[dried]] [[chillies]], soak them for 30 minutes in [[boiled]] water before removing the stalks and chopping.  If you are uncertain as to how hot this dish will be for you, don't add the seeds, reserve them, taste the sauce after 15 minutes and add them if you need more heat. Wear rubber gloves when handling [[chillies]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#prawnsnpepsi #sauce #garlic #prawns #fry #lime #chillies #tomatoes #pepsi #butter #onions </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

lovely and will be a regular favourite.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 300g unseasoned [[Pulled beef brisket]]\n| 1 can El Paso [[Refried beans|refried beans]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Taste Sensation]] [[Tex mex small [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], chopped\n| Half a [[Sweet red pepper|sweet red pepper]], deseeded and chopped\n| 6 [[Taco shells|taco shells]]\n| 150 ml [[Sour cream|sour cream]]\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\nPreheat your oven or air fryer to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Mix the used the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]].\n| Line the [[Air Fryer|air fryer]] or [[Oven tray|oven tray]] with [[Greaseproof paper|greaseproof paper]].\n| Fill the [[Taco shells|taco shells]] with the [[Meat|meat]] and [[Bean|bean]] mix\n| Arrange the chopped [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Onions|onions]] and [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] over the top.\n| Sprinkle with [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheddar cheese|cheddar                 "revisions": [

                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pupusa de Chicharron recipe Accompaniments\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#bacon #curtido #pupusadechicharron #tomatoes #toasted #masaharina #peppers #garlic #griddled #oliveoil #greenbellpepper \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A stuffed corn-tortilla, served with a spicy coleslaw called curtido. Pupusas are hand-made and thick\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 489\n|PortionCalories = 61\n|DatePublished=27th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Cheese pupusa with curtido\n|Servings = Serves 8 - Will fill about 8 pupusa\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 2 hours 20 minutes\n|PrepTime = 2 hours\n|CookTime = 20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Cheese pupusa recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Hard work</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Lots of work for street food.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nA pupusa is a stuffed corn-tortilla, usually served with a spicy coleslaw called [[curtido]].\n\nPupusas are hand-made and thick. Like all [[corn tortillas]], they are made using [[masa harina]].  They originate from El Salvador. \n\nThis is not true to the original which uses pork rinds.  This slightly healthier version is stuffed with a bacon tomato and green pepper mixture\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 8 rashers [[bacon]]\n| 2 [[cloves garlic, crushed]]\n| 4 [[tomatoes]]\n| 1 [[green bell pepper]]\n| [[Ghee]] or [[olive oil]] for [[frying]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Fry the crushed [[Garlic|garlic]] for a minute in the hot ghee or oil\n| Fry the [[bacon]] until cooked, but not crisp\n| deseed and finely chop the [[green pepper]]\n| Grind or blend the [[bacon]] and [[tomatoes]] into a rough paste\n| Stir in the chopped [[peppers]]\n| [[Corn tortilla recipe|Make the tortillas as shown here]], but don't cook them yet\n| Divide the mixture into balls, slightly larger than golf-balls and place each ball in the centre of the tortilla and press the mixture out, leaving a gap around the edge\n| Cover with another tortilla and press together to seal\n| Heat a griddle pan or heavy frying pan and wipe over with a lightly oiled kitchen towel\n| Cook each  pupusa until it is nicely [[toasted]].  This will take about 4 minutes a side\n| Keep warm while you cook the remaining pupusas\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[curtido]]\n===Variations===\n\nMake the pupusas with a combination of this, [[refried beans]] and the filling for [[Cheese pupusas]]\n===Chef's notes===\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Starters|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#bacon #curtido #pupusadechicharron #tomatoes #toasted #masaharina #peppers #garlic #griddled #oliveoil #greenbellpepper </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

I've deliberately not used a spicy sauce as the contrast between the spicy beef and the tomato soup might be interesting.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 250 g [[beef mince]] (''ground beef'')\n| 600g pot of tomato and basil soup\n| 150 g [[Cheddar cheese]], [[grated]]\n| 1 stick of [[celery]], chopped into thin crescents ''(half moons)''\n| 6 [[spring onions]] (scallions), chopped finely\n| 300g of cooked [[kidney beans]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[garlic olive oil]] or [[olive oil]] and 1 [[garlic clove, crushed]]\n| 1 green [[bell pepper]], sliced\n| 8 [[flour]] or [[corn tortillas]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]=== \n* Preheat the [[oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - Gas 4) \n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Quick beef enchiladas ready to bake.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Quick beef enchiladas ready to bake\nImage:Minced beef mixture cooked.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The filling is cooked\nImage:Served with purple broccoli.jpg|Delicious, served with [[purple broccoli]]\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a [[wok]] or [[frying]] pan, heat the [[garlic olive oil]] gently and [[fry]] the [[minced beef]], [[celery]] and the [[green peppers]] for about 5 minutes.\n| Add the beans and taco seasoning and mix well.\n| Remove from the heat and drain any excess liquid.  You don't want the mixture too wet.\n| Mix in the [[spring onions]]\n| Divide the mix into eight portions and roll up in the [[tortillas]]\n| Place in an oven proof dish\n| Pour the soup over the [[tortillas]] and gently move them around so the soup fills all the gaps\n| Sprinkle with the [[cheese]]\n| Bake for 30 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[sour cream]] and finely chopped [[chillies]]!\n===Variations===\nAny interesting soup will do. You could use or 568 lm (1 pint) strong [[beef stock]], thickened with flour or cornflour\n===Chef's noites===\nI chop and freeze leftover celery before it goes soft so I've always got a little spare\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#quickbeefenchiladas #garlicoliveoil #tortillas #celery #springonions #oliveoil #miseenplace #mincedbeef #cheddarcheese #flour #frying </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Roasting a chicken on a beer can (Modernist Cuisine)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Roasting a chicken on a beer can (Modernist Cuisine) recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #beercan #bake #beercanchicken #roastingachickenonabeercanmodernistcuisine #equipment #modernistcuisine #rosemary #thighs #sage #herbs \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=The technique here is basically to flay the chicken and then to cook the chicken very slowly, afterwards, baking very quickly on a high heat\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1070\n|PortionCalories = 267\n|DatePublished=29th November 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = After 4 hours plus the browning stage\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  5 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  5 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Roasting a chicken on a beer can Modernist Cuisine recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Beer in the butt chicken</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.9</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Almost the perfect meal</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Roasting a chicken on a beer can Modernist Cuisine 4hours.jpg|thumb|300px|right|After baking for 4 hours]]\nI've cooked [[Beer can chicken|beer can chicken]] many, many times and even cooked [[Beer can turkey|beer can turkey]] for Christmas dinner 3 years in a row so after reading ''[[Modernist Cuisine]]. The Art and Science of Cooking, Volume 1: Volume 2 - Volume 2 - Techniques and [[Equipment]]'' ISBN 978-0982761007, I was interested to try the approach they used there.\n\nThe technique is basically to flay the [[Chicken|chicken]] (separate the skin from the flesh) , cook the chicken very slowly and then to [[Bake|bake]] quickly at an intense heat to crisp the skin.\n\nI've modified their recipe slightly by adding a rub of [[Old India Taco Seasoning]], and adding a large bunch of herbs to the empty beer can and just putting 120 ml of water into the beer can so the herbs don't burn and the chicken gets a little extra moisture.\n\nAs with most of the [[Molecular gastronomy]] recipes, they are rather involved or take longer than normal though it is generally worth the extra effort.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 x 1.7 kg [3.7 lb] whole [https://www.cookipedia.co.uk/calories/chicken/bq/11#jump chicken chicken]\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Old India Taco Seasoning]]\n| A large bunch of [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]], [[Thyme|thyme]], [[Sage|sage]] and [[Rosemary|rosemary]]\n| 120 ml water\n| Empty [[Beer can|beer can]]\n| [[Grillpro Stainless Steel Chicken Roaster]] (optional)\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 100\u00b0 C (225\u00b0 F - gas \u00bc) or even lower if your oven will allow\n| Remove the [[Parson's nose|parson's nose]]\n| Starting from either end, separate the skin of the [[Chicken|chicken]] from the flesh, leaving it completely intact, being careful not to tear the skin.  When you have finished, the skin should hang from the chicken like a baggy jumper.\n| I found a very large flat spoon ideal to do this.\n| Leave the skin connected to the wings and the tips of the [[Drumsticks|drumsticks]].\n| Cut a small hole in the skin at the bottom of each leg so any juices can drain. each \n| Empty the [[Beer can|beer can]] or find a volunteer to do this for you :-)\n| Pop the [[Herbs|herbs]] into the empty [[Beer can|beer can]] and add 120 ml of water.\n| If you have a [[Grillpro Stainless Steel Chicken Roaster]],  put the can on this and sit the [[Chicken|chicken]] on the roaster.  If you don't have one, put the [[Beer can|beer can]] on a [[Roasting tray|roasting tray]] and very carefully sit the chicken on the [[Beer|beer]] can.\n| Nathan Myhrvold also suggests cutting a hole in the butt, however, the way I've flayed my [[Chicken|chicken]] that is not necessary.\n| [[Bake]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] to a core temperature of 60\u00b0 C (140\u00b0 F) when measured with a [[Digital thermometer|digital thermometer]].  This will probably take around 4 hours.\n| When core temperature has been reached, remove the bird from the [[Oven|oven]] and set to one side.\n| Set the [[Oven|oven]] to its highest temperature and let it heat for 20 minutes.\n| Make a little 'hat' of [[tin-foil]] to sit over the uppermost part of the chicken to enable even [[browning]] ands return the [[Chicken|chicken]] to the [[Oven|oven]] and [[Bake|bake]] until the skin is crisp and golden.\n| This should take around 15 to 20 minutes, but watch it like a hawk or you will have a burnt, [[Smoking|smoking]] [[Chicken|chicken]].\n| Remove from the [[Oven|oven]], carve and serve immediately\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* The Art and Science of Cooking, Volume 1: Volume 2 - Volume 2 - Techniques and [[Equipment]]'' ISBN 978-0982761007, Nathan Myhrvold with Chris Young and Maxime Bilet\n===Variations===\nBy adjusting the core temperature you can cook your preferred [[Meat|meat]] so it is at its best.\n\nFor juicy, tender white [[Meat|meat]] (the breast), use a core temperature of 60\u00b0 C (140\u00b0 F)\n\nFor succulent [[Brown|brown]] [[Meat|meat]] (legs and [[Thighs|thighs]]) aim for 65\u00b0 C (150\u00b0 F)\n\nMake these adjustments by leaving the door slightly ajar.\n\n===Chef's notes===\nAfter making this, I have to say that it was brilliant, really moist and juicy, however, that goes for any [[beer can chicken]], this distinct disadvantage of this method is that it is because of the variations in cooking time, it's not as easy to produce the finished dish at a very specific time.  I will still be cooking my beer can chickens the way I always done.\n{{Template:Beercan chicken -  See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Molecular gastronomy recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #beercan #bake #beercanchicken #roastingachickenonabeercanmodernistcuisine #equipment #modernistcuisine #rosemary #thighs #sage #herbs </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Salsa verde, a herb recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#salsaverde #sesameseeds #parsley #capers #blackpepper #oliveoil #whitewinevinegar #tinnedanchovies #foodprocessor #basil #barbecue \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A tangy dip, strongly flavoured with herbs that goes well with fish and meat and would be a good addition to a barbecue\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 370\n|PortionCalories = 92\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Salsa verde & Salsa rojo\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 5 minutes\n|PrepTime = 5 minutes\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Salsa verde recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Very herby</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Nice with grilled chicken</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nA tangy dip, strongly flavoured with [[herbs]] that goes well with fish and meat and would be a good addition to a [[barbecue]].  Don't bother making this with dried herbs!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| Handful of fresh [[parsley]]\n| Handful of fresh [[basil]]\n| 6 [[tinned anchovies]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[capers]], chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[sesame seeds]]\n| 2 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, crushed\n| 1 tablespoon [[sherry vinegar]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[white wine vinegar]]\n| 1 slice of white bread, crusts removed, broken into pieces\n| Salt and [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 150 ml [[extra virgin olive oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Remove and discard the stems from the [[parsley]]\n| Add all of the ingredients except for the olive oil and the [[sesame seeds]] and blitz in a [[food processor]] until finely chopped\n| Slowly add the [[olive oil]] until you have a thick sauce\n| Mix in the [[sesame seeds]]\n| Season to taste with [[salt]] and [[black pepper]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nThis will keep refrigerated for a day or so.\n\nTry this with fried monkfish in [[monkfish salsa verde]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#salsaverde #sesameseeds #parsley #capers #blackpepper #oliveoil #whitewinevinegar #tinnedanchovies #foodprocessor #basil #barbecue </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Don't..\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 223\n|PortionCalories = 223\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = thumb|right|Sauerkraut\n|Servings = Makes 3 litres of pickles\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 7 days, 30 minutes\n|PrepTime = 7 days, 30 minutes\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Sauerkraut.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">I make this by the Ton!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I make jars and jars of this and they keep for ages - except I always eat them.  Really good with cod and chips.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\n\n[[Sauerkraut]] is a traditional fermented vegetable food made from cabbage. This is a basic recipe that produces a tangy sauerkraut with live bacteria. \n\nDon't seal the jar until [[fermentation]] is complete as it may explode!\n\nNo cooking is required.\n\nWe have a recipe for a similar dish; [[Curtido]], a pickled relish from El Salvador and also a [[Spicy pickled cabbage|spicy pickled red cabbage recipe.]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 large (2.5 kg - 5 lb) fresh white [[cabbage]]\n| 2-3 tablespoons [[sea salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Clean and dry a large (3 litre) preserves jar and any bowls or work surfaces that you will be using\n| Quarter the [[cabbage]] and remove the core\n| Slice the [[cabbage]] finely or thickly, as you prefer.  A [[food processor]] is good for this\n| Layer the [[cabbage]] in the preserves jar,  sprinkling salt in between layers\n| Pack tightly into the jar, leaving 1cm space at the top\n| Juice should rise to top of jar as you tightly pack the [[cabbage]] in; if not, add a little bottled water\n| Don't seal the jar while it is [[fermenting]], as it will build up gas pressure and might break. Just cover with a cloth, or [[cling-wrap]]\n| The [[sauerkraut]] will be fermented in about a week. Wipe any excess liquid from around the jar, and put the lid on tightly before moving it to a cool place (e.g. the [[refrigerator]]) to mature. It is ready to eat after the first week, but will improve with age and as the bacteria slowly consume the more complex sugars in the cabbage\n}}\n===Variations===\n\n'''Add any of the following:'''\n* [[juniper berries]]\n* [[onion]]\n* [[chili]]\n* grated [[carrot]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:German recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]][[Category:Pickled]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cabbage #sauerkraut #fermenting #curtido #pickled #onion #foodprocessor #fermentation #refrigerator #litres #sauerkrautrecipe </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Sincronizada recipe",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sincronizada recipe Cheese, from Cookipedia.Co.Uk\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cheese #ham #quesadillas #tortillas #sincronizadarecipe #flourtortillas #tortilla #sandwich #grilled #masa #cheddar \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=In Mexican cuisine, the sincronizada is a tortilla-based sandwich\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2455\n|PortionCalories = 1227\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 2\n |Difficulty = 1\n |ImageComment = A \"sincronizada\", cut into wedges\n |TotalTime = 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Sincronizada recipe recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Cheese tortilla sandwich</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I like mine with extra chillies!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\nIn [[Mexican Cuisine|Mexican cuisine]], the sincronizada is a [[Tortilla|tortilla]]-based [[Sandwich|sandwich]]. They are frequently confused with [[Quesadillas|quesadillas]], due to their resemblance to \"quesadillas\" sold in the United States. (U.S. quesadillas are usually made with [[Flour tortillas|flour tortillas]] rather than molded from [[Masa|masa]] in the [[Mexican]] style).\n\nSincronizadas (so called because the top and bottom [[Tortilla|tortilla]] are \"synchronized\" together) [[Sandwich|sandwich]] ingredients between two [[Tortillas|tortillas]]. The sandwich is then [[Grilled|grilled]].\n\n=== The difference between Sincronizadas & [[quesadillas]] ===\n''This is only a rough guide, there are many, many regional differences.''\n* Sincronizadas usually include [[Ham|ham]]\n* Sincronizadas are usually made with [[Wheat flour|wheat flour]] [[tortillas]]\n* Sincronizadas are usually served flat, cut into segments\n* [[Quesadillas]] are usually made with [[corn tortillas]], though can be made with [[flour tortillas]]\n* As well as [[cheese]], [[Quesadillas]] can often contain, meat, [[refried beans]] and vegetables.\n* [[Quesadillas]] are often rolled before serving.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 soft [[Flour tortillas|flour tortillas]]\n| 1 cup [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]].\n| 70g strong [[Cheddar]]. ''Original recipes suggest [[Oaxaca cheese]] or [[Monterey Jack cheese]]''.\n| 4 slices of thinly sliced [[Ham|ham]] or [[Prosciutto|prosciutto]], cut into strips\n| 2 red [[Hot chillies|hot chillies]], de-seeded and thinly sliced (or to taste)\n|* You can use [[Chilli|chilli]] [[Sauce|sauce]] instead if you prefer\n| A few thinly cut slices of fresh [[Tomato|tomato]]\n| A few rings of thinly sliced [[Onions|onions]]\n| A handful of [[Coriander|coriander]] or [[Parsley leaves|parsley leaves]], chopped finely\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Lay two of the [[Tortillas|tortillas]] side-by-side on a flat surface and sprinkle with half of the [[Cheese|cheese]]\n| Layer the half of [[Ham|ham]] on to the [[Cheese|cheese]]\n| Distribute the remaining ingredients apart from the [[Cheese|cheese]] and [[Ham|ham]]\n| Top with the remaining [[Ham|ham]] and [[Cheese|cheese]]\n| Complete the 'sandwiches' by covering with the [[Tortillas|tortillas]]\n| On a [[Griddle|griddle]] or a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]], cook the sincronizadas, one at-a-time until the [[Tortillas|tortillas]] are lightly [[Browned|browned]] and starting to become crispy, turning once\n| Cut each sincronizada into 6 quadrants\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot with [[Guacamole|guacamole]] and a [[Green salad|green salad]]\n===Variations===\nChange the [[Cheddar cheese]] for a Mexican type of cheese that is called [[Oaxaca cheese|\"quesillo/queso oaxaca\"]] which can be easily torn into thinner strands and melts faster. \n\nI usually put some mayonnaise on the tortillas then the ham,cheese, a bit of fried beans, and cover it with the other tortilla with mayonnaise and another slice of ham. -- [[User:Pepekike]] 04:28, 21 July 2011 \n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n* [[Talk:Sincronizada_recipe|Visitor comments]] relating to this recipe\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cheese #ham #quesadillas #tortillas #sincronizadarecipe #flourtortillas #tortilla #sandwich #grilled #masa #cheddar </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sloppy Joe recipe Beef, from Cookipedia.Co.Uk\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#sloppyjoerecipe #mincedbeef #onions #tomato #breadrolls #oliveoil #chillipowder #groundbeef #peppers #sourcream #garlic \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A Sloppy Joe is an American dish of ground beef, onions, sweetened tomato sauce or ketchup and other seasonings, served on a hamburger bun\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2127\n|PortionCalories = 531\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 25 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Sloppy Joe recipe recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Way to eat chilli</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Chilli on the go.  I feel like a movie star eating this.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nA Sloppy Joe is an American dish of [[Ground beef|ground beef]], [[Onions|onions]], sweetened [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]] or [[Ketchup|ketchup]] and other seasonings, served on a hamburger bun. Contradictory lore suggests that the Original Sloppy Joe [[Sandwich]] was invented at Sloppy Joe's Bar in Key West, Florida, or by a cook named Joe at a cafe in Sioux City, Iowa, as a variation of the popular \"loose meat\" sandwich (which does not contain [[Tomato|tomato]] [[Sauce|sauce]]).\n\nThere are numerous variations of this recipe, this is my favourite.  I add lots more [[chilli]] so it becomes [[chilli con carne]] in a roll.\n===Other names===\nSloppy joes can also referred to as:\n* ''Yip Yips'' in Southern Illinois near St Louis. \n* ''Yum Yums'' in parts of the Midwest USA, particularly in Nebraska\n* ''Wimpies'' in parts of the Northeast USA, especially Northeastern Pennsylvania\n* ''Slushburgers'' in parts of the Upper Midwest, particularly in Eastern Montana and Western North Dakota\n* ''Barbecues'' in other areas of the Upper Midwest, and also in some parts of Southeastern Pennsylvania.\n* ''Taverns'' in parts of northwest Iowa and Minnesota.\n* ''Sloppy Janes'' in parts of central Minnesota.\n* '' Steamers'' in parts of Virginia, West Virginia, and Maryland.\n* ''Gulash'' (not to be confused with [[Goulash]]) in parts of the Upper Midwest.\n* ''Dynamites'' in northern Rhode Island.\n* ''Manwich'' in parts of Northern New Jersey, after the popular name brand sauce, as a distinction from the local variant also known as a \"sloppy joe\"\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 tablespoon [[Olive oil|olive oil]] for [[Frying|frying]]\n| 450 g (1 lb) [[Minced beef|minced beef]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], chopped\n| 1 small [[Sweet pepper|sweet pepper]], chopped\n| 4 tablespoons of [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e\n| 1 tablespoon [[Worcestershire sauce]]\n| 142 ml (&frac14; pint) water\n| 2 [[Cloves garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Dried oregano|dried oregano]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Cider vinegar|cider vinegar]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n}}\n'''to serve:'''\n* 4 [[Bread rolls|bread rolls]], halved\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]] to medium/high and [[Brown|brown]] the [[Minced beef|minced beef]] for 5 minutes.\n| Lower the heat to medium, add the [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a further 5 minutes.  Drain any excess [[Fat|fat]] at this stage.\n| Mix the remaining ingredients with the water and add to the pan.\n| Cook for 10 minutes or until thickened enough to just about hold together.\n| Spoon on to lightly [[Toasted|toasted]] [[Bread rolls|bread rolls]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe on their own or with one or two of the following:\n* [[Chips]]\n* [[Green salad]]\n* [[Tomato & onion salad]]\n* [[Red onion and orange salad]]\n* [[Fennel, red onion and orange salad]]\n* [[Cole-slaw|cole-slaw]]\n* [[Sour cream]]\n===See also===\n* {{ChiliConCarne}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#sloppyjoerecipe #mincedbeef #onions #tomato #breadrolls #oliveoil #chillipowder #groundbeef #peppers #sourcream #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sous-vide chili cheese turkey crown\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#turkey #onion #dry #herbs #spices #frozen #roast #defrost #parsonsnose #cheeserecipes #sageleaves\n|description=Sounds weird, but I assure you, its fabulous. If the flavours disturb you, leave the spices out and make it sage and onion\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=23rd January 2021\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 7\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  10 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  10 hours\n|TotalCalories = 1897\n|PortionCalories = 271\n|Image = [[Image:Sous vide turkey crown with roasties.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Fabulous</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Last week we did beef in this marinade and it was better than the turkey.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nSounds weird, but I assure you, it's fabulous.\n\nIf the flavours disturb you, then just leave the [[Spices|spices]] out and make it with just [[Sage|sage]] and [[Onion|onion]].\n\nI've found that it's cooked perfectly well after 5 hours, but I like to leave it for about ten hours so the flavours penetrate properly.  It won't dry out during the extended cooking time if it's cooked [[Sous-vide|sous-vide]]. This is probably the most succulent way we've found to cook turkey.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 medium [[Frozen|frozen]] [[Turkey]] Crown \n| 1 [[Onion|onion]]\n| Bunch of [[Sage leaves|sage leaves]]\n| A sprig of fresh [[Thyme leaves|thyme leaves]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Taste Sensation Chili Cheese marinade]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Thoroughly [[Defrost|defrost]] the [[Turkey|turkey]] crown in a cool place.\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Peel and chop the [[Onion|onion]]\n| Wash and [[Dry|dry]] the [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]]\n| Add the chopped [[Onion|onion]], [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Taste Sensation Chili Cheese Marinade Powder]] to the [[Sous-vide|sous-vide]] bag\n| Carefully rinse the [[Turkey|turkey]] crown in warm water and pat [[Dry|dry]] with [[Paper towels|paper towels]]\n| Using [[Poultry shears|poultry shears]] or good scissors, remove and discard the flap of fatty skin at the rear of the bird, where the [[Parson's nose]] was.\n| Add the [[Turkey|turkey]] crown to the [[Sous-vide|sous-vide]] bag and shake well to allow the [[Spices|spices]] and [[Herbs|herbs]] to be evenly distributed throughout.\n| [[Vacuum seal]] and cook in the [[Sous-vide bath|sous-vide bath]] for 10 hours at 67\u00b0 C\n| Serve immediately, no need to [[Rest|rest]] the bird when it's cooked this way.\n| The juices make a nice spicy [[Gravy|gravy]] when added 50/50 to chicken [[gravy granules]] &#128520;.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Sous vide turkey crown, carved.jpg|Carved!\nImage:Sous-vide turkey crown after ten hours.jpg|After ten hours in the bath\nImage:Nacho cheese sous-vide turkey crown.jpg| Coated with herbs and spices and ready for 10 hours in the bath\nImage:Aldi medium turkey crown.jpg | Medium turkey crown from Aldi\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nOn the day of cooking, we like to serve the [[Turkey|turkey]] as a [[Roast|roast]] with all the trimmings.  The second and third days, it's lovely with a [[Salad|salad]] or in [[Pittas|pittas]].\n===Variations===\nSlice up a whole leak and add it to the [[Sous-vide|sous-vide]] bag with lots of [[Herbs|herbs]] so the flavours permeate the [[Turkey|turkey]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide cooking]]\n[[Category:Taste Sensation recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n{{Template:Sous Vide, Smoking and Curing UK}}\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#turkey #onion #dry #herbs #spices #frozen #roast #defrost #parsonsnose #cheeserecipes #sageleaves</code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

If you've got one, then start cooking!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Pork tenderloin]] cooked [[Sous-vide|sous-vide]] is glorious.  Tender and juicy with a hint of [[Spice|spice]] and [[Herbs|herbs]].  I actually cooked this for another recipe, [[Cheatin' pork enchiladas]] as I needed pre cooked [[Tenderloin|tenderloin]].  This would be fabulous cooked as it is but if you are going to use it in another recipe, try to avoid overcooking the pork in the second recipe or you will lose the benefit of cooking [[Sous vide|sous vide]].\n[[Image:Sous vide TexMex pork tenderloin fillet vac sealed.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Vacuum sealed, ready to cook for 9 hours]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 [[Pork tenderloin fillet|pork tenderloin fillet]] (about 700g)\n| 2 bunches of [[Sage leaves|sage leaves]]\n| &#189; small [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced\n| 1 stick of celery, cut into moons\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Old India Taco Seasoning]] or a similar [[Spice|spice]] [[Blend|blend]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| If you have a [[Swiss steak|meat tenderiser]] with metal blades, stamp the tenderloin all over, on both sides.\n| Cut the [[Pork fillet|pork fillet]] into 2 pieces so it will fit into a large vacuum bag together with the [[Onion|onion]] a [[Herbs|herbs]].\n| Seal the bag at one end and add the [[Pork tenderloin|pork tenderloin]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Spices|spices]].\n| Hold the bag closed and shake well to mix.\n| Wipe the edge to be sealed with a [[Paper towel|paper towel]] to ensure it seals properly.\n| [[Vacuum seal]] the bag.  I like to seal twice at both ends, but that's just the pessimist in me!\n| Cook [[Sous vide|sous vide]] at 59\u00b0C (''138.2\u00b0F'') for up to 9 hours or at least a minimum of 3 hours.\n| Once cooked, discard the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Herbs|herbs]] and any juices.\n| If you want to [[Brown|brown]] the outside, cook in a hot pan with a little [[Butter|butter]] for a few minutes, adding an extra blast of a [[Blowtorch|blowtorch]] if you have one.\n| Slice and serve!\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you are using [[Old India Taco Seasoning]], don't add any [[Salt|salt]] or [[Pepper|pepper]] as this mix is pretty salts already.  However, without Old [[India]] [[Taco seasoning|taco seasoning]], this would be delicious with just a grind of pepper and a pinch of salt added before sealing the bag.\n{{SousVideSeeAlso}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide cooking]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#herbs #onion #spice #porktenderloin #sousvide #porkfillet #porktenderloinfillet #blowtorch #tacoseasoning #sousvidetexmexporktenderloinfillet #blend </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

Other fish varieties would work fine including [[red snapper]], [[cod]], [[bass]], [[bream]] and [[pollack]]\n[[Image:Spicy tuna burritos recipe.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Spicy tuna burritos, ready to roll!]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 175 g (6 oz) [[tuna steaks]] per person\n| 90 g (3.5 oz) [[basmati rice]]\n| 1 small [[onion]]\n| 1 teaspoon ground [[achiote seed]] ([[annatto powder]])\n| A few small dried [[chillies]], ground to a powder\n| 75 g (3 oz) flaked [[almonds]]\n| 1 400g tin chopped [[tomatoes]]\n| 85 g (3&frac12; oz) [[Cheddar cheese]], grated\n| 6 large wheat [[flour]] tortillas\n| 2 tablespoons [[olive oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Preheat the grill\n| In a small frying pan, toast the [[almonds]] until browned. Careful not to burn them!  Set aside\n| Cook the [[tuna]] for 4 minutes per side on an oiled grill tray.  When cooked, flake into a bowl and set aside\n| Rinse the [[rice]] well under cold running water\n| In a large pan, cover the [[rice]] with boiling water, return to the boil and simmer for about 8 minutes.  Drain and set aside\n| Heat the oil in a large pan and cook the [[onion]] until soft and translucent\n| Add the [[achiote powder]] and [[Chili powder|chili]] powder and cook for a few minutes\n| Add the rice and stir fry for a minute\n| Add the [[tomatoes]], stir well and then cover and simmer until most of the juice has been absorbed into the rice (about 15 minutes)\n| Warm the tortillas under a grill for a few minutes (or seconds in a microwave)\n| Stir in the cheese and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nYou can roll the [[burritos]] in the kitchen so they are ready to serve or bring the mixture to the table in a bowl and let everyone make their own.\n\nServe with wedges of [[lime]] and a green salad\n\n===Variations===\n\nMake the [[burritos]] and heat under a grill for a few minutes for an interesting change.\n\nIf you can't get [[Annatto powder|annatto powder]], try other spices such as [[cumin]] and [[paprika]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:North American recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#spicytunaburritos #tomatoes #rice #almonds #burritos #onion #tuna #annattopowder #redsnapper #basmatirice #burrito </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Succotash (Native American)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Succotash (Native American) Cooking with chillies recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#succotash #limabeans #corn #beans #squash #limejuice #vegetableoil #vegetables #garlic #favabeans #greenbeans \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Succotash is standard American fare, the addition of squash probably makes the a more traditional recipe\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1284\n|PortionCalories = 321\n|DatePublished=25th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Succotash without the squash\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 35 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Succotash.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">It's just mixed vegetables</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">1</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I've bags of these in the freezer, from Tesco's \ud83d\ude03</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Succotash]] is standard American fare, the addition of [[Squash|squash]] probably makes the a more traditional recipe.\n[[Succotash]] (from the native American Narragansett; ms\u00edckquatash, \"[[Boiled|boiled]] [[Corn|corn]] kernels\") is a food dish consisting primarily of [[Lima beans|lima beans]], [[Carrots|carrots]] and [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]], possibly including pieces of [[Cured meat|cured meat]] or [[Fish|fish]]. \n\nThis method of preparing [[Vegetables|vegetables]] became very popular during the Great Depression in the United States. It was sometimes cooked in a [[Casserole|casserole]] form, often with a light pie crust on top as in a traditional pot pie. In some parts of the American south, any mixture of [[Vegetables|vegetables]] prepared with lima [[Beans|beans]] and topped with [[Lard|lard]] or [[Butter|butter]] is called succotash. Succotash is a traditional dish of many Thanksgiving celebrations in Pennsylvania and other states. In Indiana, Succotash is made with [[Green beans|green beans]] and corn instead of lima [[Beans|beans]].\n\nOther uses of the word \"[[Succotash|succotash]]\" include its use as the catch phrase of the Warner Bros. cartoon cat Sylvester; \"Sufferin' succotash\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 20 ml [[Vegetable oil]]\n| 2 cups fresh, [[Frozen|frozen]] or drained, canned [[Corn|corn]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped finely\n| 2 medium [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]], any colour, de-seeded chopped\n| 1 or 2 fresh [[Hot chillies|hot chillies]], de-seeded and chopped into rings\n| 1 cup [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] flesh, cut into 1 cm (1/2\") cubes\n| 2 cups canned [[Lima beans]], drained\n| 2 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 1 tablespoon [[White cumin|white cumin]], freshly [[Ground|ground]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] to taste.\n| &frac12; cup [[Chicken|chicken]] or [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n}}\n'''Garnish'''\n* Bunch of finely chopped coriander leaves, stems discarded\n* Squeeze of [[lemon juice]] or [[lime juice]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat 1 tablespoon of [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] in a large pan or [[Wok|wok]] until [[Smoking|smoking]]\n| Add the [[Corn|corn]], [[Peppers|peppers]] and [[Onions|onions]] and saut\u00e9 until the onions start to take a little colour, about 6 to 7 minutes\n| Reduce the heat, add the [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Squash|squash]] cubes, [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Cumin|cumin]] and cook for about 4 minutes, stirring often.\n| Add the [[Stock|stock]] and the [[Lima beans|lima beans]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] until the [[Squash|squash]] is tender\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe garnished with [[Coriander|coriander]] and [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n===Variations===\nIf you cannot obtain [[Lima beans|lima beans]] then try [[Fava beans|fava beans]], [[Broad beans|broad beans]], [[Flageolet beans|flageolet beans]], '''Sufferin' [[Succotash|succotash]] - use any [[Beans|beans]]''' - just try the recipe!\n==See also==\n* [[Succotash (British ingredients)]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Beans]]\n[[Category:Prepared foods]]\n[[Category:Vegetables]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#succotash #limabeans #corn #beans #squash #limejuice #vegetableoil #vegetables #garlic #favabeans #greenbeans </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

Replace the lid and shake like mad to coat the sweet potatoes evenly\n| Peel and quarter the [[Red onions|red onions]] and add the the [[Lock and Lock box]].  Shake more gently this time so as not to separate the [[Onions|onions]] too much\n| Shake the mixture on to the hot [[Baking tray|baking tray]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 40 minutes\n| After 35 minutes, [[Crumble|crumble]] the [[Feta cheese|feta cheese]] over the [[Sweet potatoes|sweet potatoes]] and return to the [[Oven|oven]] for the final 5 minutes\n| Serve hot!\n}}\n===Variations===\n*Try this recipe with a variety of [[chilli sauces]]!\n*Add a [[Tomato salsa|tomato salsa]] to make a tasty [[Vegetarian|vegetarian]] [[Taco|taco]] filling.\n*Swap the [[Sweet potato|sweet potato]] for [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]].  The [[Cooking times|cooking times]] will be similar.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#sweetpotatobake #sweetpotato #redonions #bakingtray #sweetpotatoes #fetacheese #miseenplace #wahaca #tomatosalsa #crumble #driedthyme </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
